</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">When should I prefer LLM-as-a-judge over classic metrics?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Think in terms of task semantics: use judges for open-ended generation, and classic metrics for deterministic outputs or when you need hard guarantees.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/Evaluation/LLM-as-a-Judge.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/Evaluation/LLM-as-a-Judge.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">LLM-as-a-Judge</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">How do I know whether my judge is trustworthy?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Measure agreement with a small human-labeled set, track judge drift over time, and periodically re-run calibration on a fixed gold dataset.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/Evaluation/LLM-as-a-Judge.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/Evaluation/LLM-as-a-Judge.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">LLM-as-a-Judge</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What are common pitfalls?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Judge bias (preferring verbosity), sensitivity to prompt wording, and hidden coupling (judge rewards the same style it produces).<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/Evaluation/LLM-as-a-Judge.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/Evaluation/LLM-as-a-Judge.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">LLM-as-a-Judge</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Should I rely on online metrics only?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">No. Use offline evals to prevent obvious regressions and online evals to validate real-world impact.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/Evaluation/Online Evaluation and AB Tests.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/Evaluation/Online Evaluation and AB Tests.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Online Evaluation and AB Tests</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">How do I know if I'm overfitting my prompt?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">If improvements only show up on your dev set but not on a holdout set (or online metrics), you are likely tuning to that benchmark. Add paraphrased variants, segment tests, and an untouched holdout.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/Evaluation/Overfitting.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/Evaluation/Overfitting.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Overfitting</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Is overfitting the same as hallucinations?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">No. Overfitting is a generalization problem. Hallucinations are often a grounding/knowledge/control problem. They can co-occur (a fine-tune can increase hallucinations), but you treat them differently.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/Evaluation/Overfitting.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/Evaluation/Overfitting.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Overfitting</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">When should I prefer pairwise over scorecards?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">When you iterate rapidly and care about "better than baseline" more than absolute thresholds. Use scorecards when you need hard pass/fail criteria.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/Evaluation/Pairwise Comparisons.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/Evaluation/Pairwise Comparisons.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Pairwise Comparisons</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">How do I stop the rubric from rewarding verbosity?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Add a separate conciseness dimension, cap maximum acceptable length, and include counterexamples where short answers are correct.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/Evaluation/Rubric Scorecards.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/Evaluation/Rubric Scorecards.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Rubric Scorecards</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">How do I choose what to target first?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Pick the failures that break trust or create real risk (hallucinations in high-stakes answers, data leakage, unsafe tool actions).<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/Evaluation/Targeted Evals.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/Evaluation/Targeted Evals.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Targeted Evals</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><h3>Prompting</h3><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is Prompting?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Prompts play a key role in generating useful and accurate information from AI language models. Learning how to write better prompts — "Prompt Engineering" — unlocks the full potential of these models by guiding their behavior, improving output quality, and reducing inaccuracies.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/Prompting/Prompting.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/Prompting/Prompting.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Prompting</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Which prompt-level controls reduce prompt-injection risk for an internal assistant that reads company documents?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Separate system instructions from user content and never allow user text to override system rules.<br>
Constrain outputs (schema or explicit format), avoid tool access unless necessary, and add deterministic checks.<br>
Treat retrieval content as untrusted input and apply allowlists for tools.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/Prompting/Prompting.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/Prompting/Prompting.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Prompting</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is Role Prompting?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Role <a data-tooltip-position="top" aria-label="Prompting" data-href="Prompting" href="Prompting" class="internal-link" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">prompting</a> is a technique that involves assigning specific roles to the LLM (Large Language Model) to control the style, tone, and quality of AI-generated text. By instructing the AI to adopt a particular role or perspective, you can influence how it approaches a task and the characteristics of its ou<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/Prompting/Role Prompting.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/Prompting/Role Prompting.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Role Prompting</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Why does few-shot prompting help with structured outputs?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Because the examples demonstrate the exact input-to-output mapping and formatting. The model often follows the demonstrated pattern more reliably than a purely textual description of the desired format.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/Prompting/Showing Examples.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/Prompting/Showing Examples.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Showing Examples</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><h3>RAG</h3><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Why should advanced RAG patterns be introduced incrementally instead of all at once?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Each pattern adds independent failure modes and observability needs. Incremental rollout isolates impact, allows A/B measurement against baseline, and prevents compounding complexity from masking root causes. Start with the pattern that addresses your highest-frequency failure mode.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/RAG.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/RAG.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">RAG</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">When is Graph RAG a better fit than plain vector retrieval?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">When answers require explicit entity relations, dependency paths, or multi-hop joins that are hard to recover from independent text chunks. Examples: compliance tracing across policy documents, architecture dependency analysis, supply chain impact assessment. Skip Graph RAG for simple fact lookups where vector similarity suffices.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/RAG.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/RAG.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">RAG</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">How does Adaptive RAG reduce cost without sacrificing accuracy on complex queries?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">A query complexity classifier routes simple queries to no-retrieval or single-pass RAG (cheap and fast) and reserves iterative multi-hop retrieval for the complex tail. Since most production queries are simple, the average cost drops significantly while complex queries still get full retrieval. Misclassification cost is asymmetric — err toward the more capable strategy when uncertain.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/RAG.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/RAG.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">RAG</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">A team's aggregate Recall@5 improves after a pipeline change, but a specific customer reports worse answers. What is the most likely evaluation failure?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">The evaluation is not sliced by meaningful segments. Aggregate metrics average across all query types and tenants, masking localized regressions. The fix is to evaluate per segment (tenant, language, query cluster, document type) and flag any segment that degrades beyond the threshold, even when the aggregate improves. This is the most common RAG evaluation failure in production.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Evaluation.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Evaluation.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Evaluation</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Why are relative regression thresholds preferable to absolute quality targets for RAG release gates?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Absolute thresholds are brittle across corpus changes, model updates, and workload shifts. A threshold set during initial launch becomes meaningless after the corpus doubles or the query distribution shifts. Relative thresholds (no more than N% regression from baseline) adapt automatically because the baseline tracks the current system state. They also prevent the failure mode where a team sets an ambitious absolute target, cannot reach it, and disables the gate entirely.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Evaluation.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Evaluation.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Evaluation</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">When should a team invest in building a human-annotated golden evaluation set versus relying on synthetic QA generation?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Synthetic generation bootstraps evaluation quickly and covers breadth, but LLM-generated questions cluster around patterns the model finds easy to generate — missing adversarial cases, ambiguous queries, and domain-specific edge cases. A golden set is worth the investment when the RAG system serves high-stakes decisions (medical, legal, financial) where evaluation failures have direct business or safety impact. In practice, use synthetic generation for broad coverage and a smaller golden set for regression gating on known failure modes.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Evaluation.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Evaluation.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Evaluation</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Why does parent-child chunking often improve answer completeness over child-only retrieval?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Child chunks maximize retrieval precision — small, focused units match specific queries well. But child-only context can miss adjacent constraints that the answer depends on (e.g., a policy rule in one child and its exception in a sibling). Parent expansion restores the surrounding context during generation, reducing partial or decontextualized answers. The tradeoff is increased context size and potential noise from the broader parent span.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Chunking.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Chunking.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Chunking</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">When should a team move from recursive to structure-aware chunking?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Move when retrieval errors consistently trace back to broken structural units — split tables, bisected code blocks, or separated clause/exception pairs. Recursive splitting respects paragraph boundaries but is blind to document-specific structures. Structure-aware chunking preserves those units at the cost of format-specific parser investment and ongoing parser maintenance.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Chunking.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Chunking.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Chunking</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Why is semantic chunking not always superior to simpler rule-based approaches?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Semantic chunking places boundaries at actual topic shifts, which sounds ideal. But it requires embedding every span during ingestion (high cost), the similarity threshold is sensitive to embedding model and domain (tuning burden), and threshold instability can cause over-fragmentation or oversized chunks. For documents with reliable structural markers (headings, sections), recursive or structure-aware chunking achieves similar boundary quality at a fraction of the ingestion cost.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Chunking.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Chunking.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Chunking</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Why can dense-only retrieval underperform on technical support workloads?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Support workloads often include exact lexical constraints such as error codes, version strings, and SKU IDs. Dense retrieval captures semantic similarity but can miss those exact tokens, reducing retrieval precision.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Retrieval.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Retrieval.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Retrieval</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Why does retrieval require metadata filters even when semantic matching is strong?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Semantic relevance does not enforce authorization boundaries. Without tenant and ACL filters, retrieval can return context that is relevant but unauthorized.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Retrieval.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Retrieval.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Retrieval</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Why is citation forcing a necessary but insufficient control?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Citation tags create traceability, but models can still attach weak or irrelevant citations. A separate verification pass must confirm claim-to-evidence support.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Grounding.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Grounding.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Grounding</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">When should grounding checks block the final answer?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Block when any material claim lacks supporting evidence, when citations are unresolved, or when sources conflict without clear resolution.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Grounding.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Grounding.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Grounding</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Why should retrieval cache keys be based on processed query text instead of raw embeddings?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Processed query text and transformation version are deterministic, auditable, and stable across embedding model upgrades. Raw embedding bytes are opaque, change with every model swap, and make cache invalidation on model upgrade impossible without full cache flush. Keying on processed text also aligns cache correctness with the query translation pipeline — if the translation changes, the key changes automatically.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Caching.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Caching.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Caching</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Why is response caching riskier than embedding caching?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Embedding is a pure function: same text plus same model always produces the same vector. Response generation depends on the system prompt template, the retrieved evidence (which changes with index updates), the user's permissions, and the model version — all mutable. A cached response can become wrong when any of these inputs change without cache invalidation. Embedding cache entries only go stale when the source text or model version changes, which are infrequent and structurally detectable.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Caching.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Caching.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Caching</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">When is semantic caching safe to deploy, and when should it be avoided?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Semantic caching is safe when the domain is narrow, queries are repetitive, false positives have low cost, and you can calibrate a reliable similarity threshold on a held-out set. It should be avoided in high-stakes domains (medical, legal, financial) where a wrong cached answer causes harm, in multi-turn conversations where context changes the correct answer, and when the query distribution is too diverse to find a threshold that balances hit rate against false-positive rate.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Caching.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Caching.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Caching</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Why is fine-tuning a weak first move for a fast-changing knowledge base?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Weight updates are slower and less transparent than retrieval updates. Frequent factual changes fit retrieval pipelines better because documents and indexes can be updated without retraining.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/RAG vs Fine-Tuning.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/RAG vs Fine-Tuning.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">RAG vs Fine-Tuning</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">When is a combined RAG + fine-tuning stack justified?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Use combined architecture when retrieval already provides correct evidence but output behavior still fails requirements such as structure, policy adherence, or domain-specific response style.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/RAG vs Fine-Tuning.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/RAG vs Fine-Tuning.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">RAG vs Fine-Tuning</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">A retrieval system uses <code>text-embedding-3-small</code> with 1536 dimensions. Latency is within SLA but storage costs are high. How would you reduce costs without significant recall degradation?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Use the <code>dimensions</code> parameter to truncate to 256 or 512 dimensions. Because <code>text-embedding-3-small</code> is trained with Matryoshka objectives, any prefix of the vector is independently meaningful. Truncation to 256 dims reduces storage by ~6x and speeds up ANN search proportionally. Validate by comparing recall@k on your evaluation set at 256, 512, and 1536 dimensions — MRL models can retain strong retrieval quality at reduced dimensions, but the actual degradation is model-specific and corpus-dependent. If recall drops unacceptably, use a two-stage approach: retrieve at reduced dimensions, then re-rank candidates using full-dimensional vectors.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Embeddings.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Embeddings.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Embeddings</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">A team switches from <code>ada-002</code> to <code>text-embedding-3-large</code> and recall drops on 20% of queries despite the new model scoring higher on MTEB. What is the most likely cause?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">The team is serving queries against vectors embedded with the old model. Different embedding models produce vectors in different geometric spaces — cosine similarity between <code>ada-002</code> vectors and <code>text-embedding-3-large</code> vectors is meaningless. The fix is to re-embed the entire corpus with the new model. This is also why embedding caches must key by model name + version.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Embeddings.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Embeddings.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Embeddings</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">When is domain-finetuning the embedding model justified over improving chunking or retrieval?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Finetuning is justified when retrieval failures are specifically caused by semantic mismatches on domain terminology — queries and relevant documents contain the same domain concepts but land far apart in vector space. If failures trace to split logical units (chunking issue), missing metadata filters (retrieval pipeline issue), or query ambiguity (query translation issue), finetuning the embedding model will not help. Diagnose by examining the top-k retrieved chunks for failed queries: if semantically relevant chunks exist but rank low, the embedding model is the bottleneck.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Embeddings.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Embeddings.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Embeddings</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Why does query translation often improve recall but sometimes hurt precision?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Additional query variants increase coverage, but weak variants can pull related yet irrelevant documents. Precision drops unless fusion and reranking suppress noisy candidates.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Query Translation.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Query Translation.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Query Translation</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">When is decomposition a better choice than plain multi-query?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Decomposition is better when the original query contains distinct sub-problems that need separate evidence retrieval and structured synthesis.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Query Translation.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Query Translation.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Query Translation</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Why can generation quality regress even if retrieval metrics improve?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Better retrieval recall can increase context volume and noise. Without tighter context assembly and prompt constraints, the model may attend to weaker evidence and produce less precise answers.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Generation.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Generation.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Generation</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">When should abstention be part of generation logic?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Include abstention when wrong answers are costly and evidence can be missing or conflicting. Abstention is a controlled failure mode that preserves trust.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Generation.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Generation.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Generation</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Why should monitoring dashboards be segmented, not only global?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">Global aggregates hide localized regressions. Segmenting by tenant, domain, or query cluster reveals failures that impact real users but disappear in overall averages.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Monitoring.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Monitoring.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Monitoring</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Why can latency-only SLO tracking be misleading for RAG?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<p dir="auto">A system can meet latency targets while serving lower-quality or ungrounded answers. Monitoring must pair speed with quality and grounding metrics.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Monitoring.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/LLM/RAG/Monitoring.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Monitoring</a></em></p>
</div></div></div><h2 id="11-ai-ml-machine-learning">Machine Learning</h2><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">How should an ML pipeline be designed to ship weekly batch churn scoring now while preserving a path to real-time scoring later?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<ul>
<li dir="auto">Start with batch to ship value, but define a stable feature contract and a single preprocessing implementation shared by batch and online</li>
<li dir="auto">Store features and predictions with versioned schema so you can backtest and replay later</li>
<li dir="auto">Use a model registry with stage promotion and rollback, and keep training code runnable in CI</li>
<li dir="auto">Plan the online boundary now: which features are available at request time and which require async enrichment</li>
<li dir="auto">Add monitoring from day one so you have drift and label delay visibility before moving to real time<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/Machine Learning/Machine Learning.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/Machine Learning/Machine Learning.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Machine Learning</a></em></li>
</ul>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What should be checked first when a binary classifier shows 98 percent accuracy but support tickets rise, and which metric should be optimized next?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<ul>
<li dir="auto">Check class balance and the confusion matrix; high accuracy can hide poor recall on the minority class</li>
<li dir="auto">Inspect label quality and leakage sources, especially time based joins and post event signals</li>
<li dir="auto">Pick metrics based on cost: optimize precision if false positives are expensive, recall if misses are expensive, or use PR AUC for heavy imbalance</li>
<li dir="auto">Tune the decision threshold using a cost curve or expected value, not the default 0.5</li>
<li dir="auto">Run slice based evaluation to find the segments where the model fails and decide whether to collect more data or add features<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/Machine Learning/Machine Learning.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/Machine Learning/Machine Learning.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Machine Learning</a></em></li>
</ul>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What tradeoffs and rollout plan are appropriate when the best model exceeds a strict API latency budget?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<ul>
<li dir="auto">Measure end to end latency budget including preprocessing, network, and tail latencies, then decide if you can meet SLO with scaling or caching</li>
<li dir="auto">Consider a smaller model, distillation, quantization, or a two stage setup where a cheap model gates the expensive one</li>
<li dir="auto">Use canary or A B rollout with guardrails on latency and key business metrics, plus automated rollback</li>
<li dir="auto">Keep a safe fallback decision path, such as a baseline model or rules, for overload and error conditions</li>
<li dir="auto">Align evaluation with production: test on representative traffic and monitor training serving skew after launch<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/Machine Learning/Machine Learning.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/Machine Learning/Machine Learning.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Machine Learning</a></em></li>
</ul>
</div></div></div><h3>Evaluation</h3><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">When should you distrust a single evaluation metric?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<ul>
<li dir="auto">When the metric does not encode the cost asymmetry of the decision, for example accuracy on imbalanced classes</li>
<li dir="auto">When the test set does not represent production traffic, for example random split on time-dependent data</li>
<li dir="auto">When the metric looks good overall but fails on critical slices or cohorts</li>
<li dir="auto">When the metric is a ranking metric but you need calibrated probabilities for downstream logic<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/Machine Learning/Evaluation/Evaluation.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/Machine Learning/Evaluation/Evaluation.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Evaluation</a></em></li>
</ul>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What does ROC-AUC measure?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<ul>
<li dir="auto">It measures ranking quality across thresholds.</li>
<li dir="auto">A higher ROC-AUC means positives usually get higher scores than negatives.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/Machine Learning/Evaluation/ROC-AUC and PR-AUC.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/Machine Learning/Evaluation/ROC-AUC and PR-AUC.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">ROC-AUC and PR-AUC</a></em></li>
</ul>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">When should I use PR-AUC instead of ROC-AUC?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<ul>
<li dir="auto">Use PR-AUC when positives are rare, like fraud or anomaly detection.</li>
<li dir="auto">PR-AUC shows how precision changes as recall increases, which is key when false positives are costly.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/Machine Learning/Evaluation/ROC-AUC and PR-AUC.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/Machine Learning/Evaluation/ROC-AUC and PR-AUC.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">ROC-AUC and PR-AUC</a></em></li>
</ul>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Why can high accuracy be misleading on imbalanced data?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<ul>
<li dir="auto">If negatives dominate, a model can predict mostly negatives and still get high accuracy.</li>
<li dir="auto">Check PR-AUC, precision, and recall to understand real positive-class performance.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/Machine Learning/Evaluation/ROC-AUC and PR-AUC.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/Machine Learning/Evaluation/ROC-AUC and PR-AUC.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">ROC-AUC and PR-AUC</a></em></li>
</ul>
</div></div></div><h3>Types</h3><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What is the recommendation when RL is proposed for a one-step fraud decision with reliable labels?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<ul>
<li dir="auto">Ship a supervised baseline first and quantify decision quality at the operating threshold.</li>
<li dir="auto">Document why RL complexity (exploration, delayed reward modeling) is unnecessary here.</li>
<li dir="auto">Reserve RL only if the objective shifts to multistep policy optimization.</li>
<li dir="auto">Compare implementation cost, safety risk, and monitoring overhead explicitly.</li>
<li dir="auto">Why: RL adds operational risk without clear benefit for one-step labeled prediction.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/Machine Learning/Types/Reinforcement Learning.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/Machine Learning/Types/Reinforcement Learning.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Reinforcement Learning</a></em></li>
</ul>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">How should an RL policy be debugged when metrics improve but customer satisfaction drops?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<ul>
<li dir="auto">Audit reward function terms against true business outcomes and constraints.</li>
<li dir="auto">Inspect trajectories where policy gains reward through undesirable shortcuts.</li>
<li dir="auto">Add safety constraints and penalty shaping for harmful behaviors.</li>
<li dir="auto">Run controlled canary traffic with rollback triggers on customer-impact metrics.</li>
<li dir="auto">Why: proxy reward optimization can diverge from real objectives if constraints are incomplete.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/Machine Learning/Types/Reinforcement Learning.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/Machine Learning/Types/Reinforcement Learning.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Reinforcement Learning</a></em></li>
</ul>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What should be investigated when pretraining loss improves but downstream retrieval quality does not?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<ul>
<li dir="auto">Verify that the proxy objective aligns with the downstream task semantics.</li>
<li dir="auto">Inspect training data contamination and duplicate-heavy corpora effects.</li>
<li dir="auto">Evaluate embedding quality with retrieval-focused metrics, not only pretraining loss.</li>
<li dir="auto">Compare against a supervised-only baseline on the same evaluation slices.</li>
<li dir="auto">Audit augmentation and negative sampling choices for shortcut learning.</li>
<li dir="auto">Why: pretraining metrics can improve while transferable representation quality stays flat.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/Machine Learning/Types/Self-Supervised Learning.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/Machine Learning/Types/Self-Supervised Learning.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Self-Supervised Learning</a></em></li>
</ul>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">How should the tradeoff between more pretraining and earlier fine-tuning be decided under limited labels and compute?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<ul>
<li dir="auto">Start with a small pretraining run and measure downstream gain per compute unit.</li>
<li dir="auto">Stop pretraining when marginal downstream lift plateaus on validation slices.</li>
<li dir="auto">Allocate compute to fine-tuning and evaluation if transfer gain is small.</li>
<li dir="auto">Keep reproducible checkpoints to compare different cutover points.</li>
<li dir="auto">Why: compute should be optimized for end-task value, not proxy-task progress.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/Machine Learning/Types/Self-Supervised Learning.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/Machine Learning/Types/Self-Supervised Learning.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Self-Supervised Learning</a></em></li>
</ul>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What should be done next if pseudo-labeling raises overall accuracy but lowers minority-class recall?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<ul>
<li dir="auto">Inspect pseudo-label precision per class, not only global accuracy.</li>
<li dir="auto">Raise thresholds for noisy classes and rebalance sampling weights.</li>
<li dir="auto">Add class-conditional calibration before accepting pseudo-labels.</li>
<li dir="auto">Re-run evaluation on minority-heavy slices with fixed supervised baseline.</li>
<li dir="auto">Keep rollback criteria based on business-costed recall targets.</li>
<li dir="auto">Why: pseudo-labeling often amplifies majority classes unless explicitly constrained.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/Machine Learning/Types/Semi-Supervised Learning.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/Machine Learning/Types/Semi-Supervised Learning.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Semi-Supervised Learning</a></em></li>
</ul>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Should a supervised-only baseline be removed after pseudo-labeling gains?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<ul>
<li dir="auto">Keep the supervised-only baseline as a safety and regression reference.</li>
<li dir="auto">Compare uplift across multiple time windows to detect drift in pseudo-label quality.</li>
<li dir="auto">Use baseline deltas to decide when to retrain or tighten thresholds.</li>
<li dir="auto">Retire the baseline only after long-term stability and slice-level consistency.</li>
<li dir="auto">Why: without a trusted baseline, noise accumulation is hard to detect early.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/Machine Learning/Types/Semi-Supervised Learning.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/Machine Learning/Types/Semi-Supervised Learning.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Semi-Supervised Learning</a></em></li>
</ul>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">What should be checked first when a fraud model has strong offline ROC-AUC but production loss increases after deployment?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<ul>
<li dir="auto">Verify leakage by auditing whether any training feature uses post-event information.</li>
<li dir="auto">Compare train, validation, and production distributions for key features and class balance.</li>
<li dir="auto">Inspect threshold calibration against business cost, not just AUC.</li>
<li dir="auto">Review label latency and stale ground-truth pipelines.</li>
<li dir="auto">Check slice-level metrics for high-value segments where loss is concentrated.</li>
<li dir="auto">Why: global metrics can hide operational failures caused by leakage, calibration drift, or segment skew.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/Machine Learning/Types/Supervised Learning.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/Machine Learning/Types/Supervised Learning.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Supervised Learning</a></em></li>
</ul>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">How should the decision be made between collecting 20k more labels and training a larger model now?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<ul>
<li dir="auto">Measure current label quality using agreement rates and error audits.</li>
<li dir="auto">Estimate expected uplift from better labels versus model capacity via ablation.</li>
<li dir="auto">Check whether current errors are data-limited or representation-limited.</li>
<li dir="auto">Compare cost and timeline of labeling versus training/inference expansion.</li>
<li dir="auto">Prefer the option that improves the highest-cost failure slices first.</li>
<li dir="auto">Why: supervised systems are often bottlenecked by data quality before model size.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/Machine Learning/Types/Supervised Learning.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/Machine Learning/Types/Supervised Learning.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Supervised Learning</a></em></li>
</ul>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">How do you determine whether k-means results are usable when different seeds produce different clusters?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<ul>
<li dir="auto">Run multiple seeds and compare stability with adjusted Rand index or similar overlap metrics.</li>
<li dir="auto">Evaluate whether clusters remain meaningful to domain experts across runs.</li>
<li dir="auto">Validate downstream utility, for example policy lift or targeting precision.</li>
<li dir="auto">Check sensitivity to feature scaling and distance metric assumptions.</li>
<li dir="auto">Prefer the simplest configuration that is stable and operationally interpretable.</li>
<li dir="auto">Why: unstable clusters usually indicate weak signal or overfitting to initialization noise.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/Machine Learning/Types/Unsupervised Learning.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/Machine Learning/Types/Unsupervised Learning.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Unsupervised Learning</a></em></li>
</ul>
</div></div></div><div><div data-callout-metadata="" data-callout-fold="-" data-callout="question" class="callout is-collapsible is-collapsed node-insert-event"><div class="callout-title" dir="auto"><div class="callout-icon"><svg width="16" height="16"></svg></div><div class="callout-title-inner">Should unsupervised learning be the starting point for customer segmentation when churn labels already exist?</div><div class="callout-fold is-collapsed"><svg xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" width="24" height="24" viewBox="0 0 24 24" fill="none" stroke="currentColor" stroke-width="2" stroke-linecap="round" stroke-linejoin="round" class="svg-icon lucide-chevron-down"><path d="m6 9 6 6 6-6"></path></svg></div></div><div class="callout-content" style="display: none;">
<ul>
<li dir="auto">Start with a supervised churn baseline to quantify immediate business impact.</li>
<li dir="auto">Use clustering as a complementary lens for exploration and cohort discovery.</li>
<li dir="auto">Test whether cluster features improve supervised metrics or intervention design.</li>
<li dir="auto">Avoid replacing a known target task with unsupervised objectives by default.</li>
<li dir="auto">Why: when labels exist, supervised learning usually maps more directly to outcomes.<br>
<em><a class="internal-link" data-href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/Machine Learning/Types/Unsupervised Learning.md" href="Software Engineering/11 AI &amp; ML/Machine Learning/Types/Unsupervised Learning.md" target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow">Unsupervised Learning</a></em></li>
</ul>
</div></div></div>
